<p><b>Sheffield station</b>, formerly <b>Pond Street</b><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> and later <b>Sheffield Midland</b>, is a combined <a href="/wiki/Railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway station">railway station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tram_stop" title="Tram stop">tram stop</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, and the busiest station in <a href="/wiki/South_Yorkshire" title="South Yorkshire">South Yorkshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Adjacent is <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_station#Supertram_stop" title="Sheffield station">Sheffield station/Sheffield Hallam University</a> <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Supertram" title="Sheffield Supertram">Sheffield Supertram</a> stop. In 2017-18, the station was the 43rd-busiest in the UK, and the 15th-busiest outside London.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The station is currently being considered as a stop for the <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">High Speed 2</a> (HS2) rail project.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1870_-_1960">1870 - 1960</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1870 - 1960">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Railway_Station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Sheffield_Railway_Station.jpg/220px-Sheffield_Railway_Station.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Sheffield_Railway_Station.jpg/330px-Sheffield_Railway_Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Sheffield_Railway_Station.jpg/440px-Sheffield_Railway_Station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3192" data-file-height="1836" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Railway_Station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The stone façade of Sheffield station, added in 1905. The <a href="/wiki/Park_Hill,_Sheffield" title="Park Hill, Sheffield">Park Hill</a> flats are in the background.</div></div></div>
<p>The station was opened in 1870 by the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Railway" title="Midland Railway">Midland Railway</a> to the designs of the company architect <a href="/wiki/John_Holloway_Sanders" title="John Holloway Sanders">John Holloway Sanders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> It was the fifth and last station to be built in Sheffield city centre.
</p><p>The station was built on the 'New Line', which ran between Grimesthorpe Junction, on the former <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_and_Rotherham_Railway" title="Sheffield and Rotherham Railway">Sheffield and Rotherham Railway</a>, and Tapton Junction, just north of <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield" title="Chesterfield">Chesterfield</a>. This line replaced the Midland Railway's previous route, the 'old road', to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, which ran from <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wicker_railway_station" title="Sheffield Wicker railway station">Sheffield Wicker</a> via <a href="/wiki/Rotherham_Masborough_railway_station" title="Rotherham Masborough railway station">Rotherham</a>.
</p><p>The new line and station were built despite some controversy and opposition locally. The Duke of Norfolk, who owned land in the area, insisted that the southern approach be in a tunnel and the land known as The Farm landscaped to prevent the line being seen. Some years later the tunnel was opened out into a cutting. <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_City_Council" title="Sheffield City Council">Sheffield Corporation</a> was so concerned about the eastern side of the city being cut off from the city centre that it insisted that public access be preserved across the railway site<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Railway_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_505748.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Railway_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_505748.jpg/220px-Railway_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_505748.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Railway_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_505748.jpg/330px-Railway_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_505748.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Railway_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_505748.jpg/440px-Railway_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_505748.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Railway_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_505748.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The interior stonework and iron roof on the station concourse</div></div></div>
<p>The station and Pond Street Goods Depot opened on a damp and cold day without any celebrations. There were originally different passenger entrances for each class. The original station buildings have been preserved and are between island platforms 2 to 5.
</p><p>The station was given two extra platforms and a new frontage in 1905 at a cost of £215,000 (equivalent to £22,680,000&#32;in 2018).<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-UK_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-UK-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The enlargements consisted of creating an island platform out of the old platform 1 and building a new platform 1 and a new entrance. These works were overseen by the Chief Architect to the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Railway" title="Midland Railway">Midland Railway</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Trubshaw" title="Charles Trubshaw">Charles Trubshaw</a>.
</p><p>Offices were built at the north end of the 300 feet (91&#160;m) long carriageway rooftop. A large parcels office was built to the south of the main buildings. Two footbridges connected the platforms, the one to the north for passengers, the one to the south for station staff and parcels. The tracks were covered by two overall roofs. The older and larger spanned platforms 5 and 6, and an identical structure can still be viewed today at <a href="/wiki/Bath_Green_Park_railway_station" title="Bath Green Park railway station">Bath Green Park railway station</a>; the other platforms 1 and 2. Wartime damage put the roofs beyond economic repair; hence, they were removed in the autumn of 1956 and replaced by low-level awnings.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1960_-_2002">1960 - 2002</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1960 - 2002">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 1960s saw the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_45" title="British Rail Class 45">Class 45</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_46" title="British Rail Class 46">Class 46</a> diesel-electric engines, known as <i>Peaks</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sheaf_House" title="Sheaf House">Sheaf House</a> was built in 1965<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> adjacent to the station to house <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Rail</a>'s Sheffield Division headquarters. As part of the reconstruction of the area as the "Gateway to Sheffield", it was demolished in early 2006. In 1970 Sheffield's other main station, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Victoria_railway_station" title="Sheffield Victoria railway station">Sheffield Victoria</a>, was closed and its remaining services, from Penistone, were diverted until 1981 via a cumbersome reversal. The Pullman service between Sheffield Victoria and London King's Cross, including the morning and evening <i><a href="/wiki/Master_Cutler_(train)" title="Master Cutler (train)">Master Cutler</a></i> now ran onto the East Coast Main Line via Retford from Sheffield Midland instead. This was the third route used by the train of that name; originally it had run to <a href="/wiki/Marylebone_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Marylebone railway station">London Marylebone</a>. The station was resignalled in 1972, and its track layout remodelled. <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Rail</a> introduced the <a href="/wiki/InterCity_125" title="InterCity 125">High Speed Train</a> (HST) to Sheffield on the Midland Main Line in 1984. The cross-country services had seen the introduction of the HSTs in 1982. On 21 December 1991, the station was flooded by the <a href="/wiki/River_Sheaf" title="River Sheaf">River Sheaf</a>, which flows under it. A log that was part of the debris commemorates the event on platform 5. In 1991 construction of the new <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Supertram" title="Sheffield Supertram">Supertram</a> network began and by late 1994 Sheffield Midland was connected to the network, after the opening of the line between <a href="/wiki/Fitzalan_Square" title="Fitzalan Square">Fitzalan Square</a> in the city centre and Spring Lane, to the east of the station.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2002_-_present">2002 - present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2002 - present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Platform_6_and_7_sheffield_station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Platform_6_and_7_sheffield_station.jpg/220px-Platform_6_and_7_sheffield_station.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="101" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Platform_6_and_7_sheffield_station.jpg/330px-Platform_6_and_7_sheffield_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Platform_6_and_7_sheffield_station.jpg/440px-Platform_6_and_7_sheffield_station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1492" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Platform_6_and_7_sheffield_station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Trains" title="East Midlands Trains">East Midlands Trains</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Station_concourse.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Sheffield_Station_concourse.JPG/220px-Sheffield_Station_concourse.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Sheffield_Station_concourse.JPG/330px-Sheffield_Station_concourse.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Sheffield_Station_concourse.JPG/440px-Sheffield_Station_concourse.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Station_concourse.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The station concourse, post- redevelopment.</div></div></div>
<p>In 2002, <a href="/wiki/Midland_Mainline" title="Midland Mainline">Midland Mainline</a>, as the main <a href="/wiki/Train_operating_company" title="Train operating company">train operating company</a> of the station, instigated a major regeneration of Sheffield station. Prior to this, a taxi rank was located inside what is now the main concourse and the new entrance hall. The stone <a href="/wiki/Facade" title="Facade">façade</a> of the station was <a href="/wiki/Abrasive_blasting" title="Abrasive blasting">sandblasted</a> and its archways filled with unobstructed windows to improve views both from inside and out.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Other changes included the improvement of platform surfaces and the addition of a pedestrian bridge connecting the station concourse with the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Supertram" title="Sheffield Supertram">Sheffield Supertram</a> stop at the far side of the station.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To coincide with the regeneration of the station, <a href="/wiki/Sheaf_Square" title="Sheaf Square">Sheaf Square</a> was rebuilt as part of a project designed to create the Gateway to Sheffield. The station and the square form part of a route that leads passengers through the square past the 262.5 feet (80.0&#160;m) Cutting Edge water feature, up <a href="/wiki/Howard_Street_(Sheffield)" title="Howard Street (Sheffield)">Howard Street</a> and into the <a href="/wiki/Heart_of_the_City_(development)" class="mw-redirect" title="Heart of the City (development)">Heart of the City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> This Gateway to Sheffield won the Project of the Year Award in the 2006 National Rail Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 November 2007, <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Trains" title="East Midlands Trains">East Midlands Trains</a>, an amalgamation of Midland Mainline and part of <a href="/wiki/Central_Trains" title="Central Trains">Central Trains</a>, took over the management of the station.
</p><p>In December 2009, following the restoration of the station, a new <a href="/wiki/Public_house" class="mw-redirect" title="Public house">pub</a>, the Sheffield Tap, opened next to platform 1B.<sup id="cite_ref-thestar.co.uk_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thestar.co.uk-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The room, located within the main station building, had been used as a store room for 35 years but was used for much longer as a bar and <a href="/wiki/Restaurant" title="Restaurant">restaurant</a>, catering for <a href="/wiki/First_class_travel" title="First class travel">first class</a> passengers since 1904.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The bar is noteworthy for its restored early 20th century interior and its selection of quality cask ales and beers from around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-thestar.co.uk_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thestar.co.uk-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Since opening, the bar has won the National Railway Heritage Award and the <a href="/wiki/Cask_ale" title="Cask ale">Cask Ale</a> pub of the year award.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2010, East Midland Trains initiated £10 million worth of improvements to its stations. Sheffield received renovated waiting rooms, toilet facilities and upgraded security systems amongst its improvements.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
A new first class lounge on platform 5, part of these improvements, opened on 18 January 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The lounge was opened by the <a href="/wiki/Master_Cutler" title="Master Cutler">Master Cutler</a> Professor Bill Speirs who was joined by 50 top business leaders from Sheffield and the surrounding area.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Station_footbridge_controversy">Station footbridge controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Station footbridge controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_railway_station_-_DSC07409.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Sheffield_railway_station_-_DSC07409.JPG/220px-Sheffield_railway_station_-_DSC07409.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Sheffield_railway_station_-_DSC07409.JPG/330px-Sheffield_railway_station_-_DSC07409.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Sheffield_railway_station_-_DSC07409.JPG/440px-Sheffield_railway_station_-_DSC07409.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_railway_station_-_DSC07409.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The bridge at the centre of the controversy</div></div></div>
<p>In 2008, East Midlands Trains revealed its intention to restrict access to parts of the station by installing <a href="/wiki/Ticket_barriers" class="mw-redirect" title="Ticket barriers">ticket barriers</a> to try to prevent passengers from travelling without a ticket. This proposal met with widespread opposition from residents and Council members because the footbridge would be closed off to non-ticket holders, severing a popular <a href="/wiki/Thoroughfare" title="Thoroughfare">thoroughfare</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Norfolk Park">Norfolk Park</a> residential area and the Supertram stop on one side, to the station travel centre, the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Interchange" title="Sheffield Interchange">bus interchange</a>, the city centre and the city centre campus of <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Hallam_University" title="Sheffield Hallam University">Sheffield Hallam University</a> on the other. On 6 May 2009, East Midlands Trains implemented its proposal, using temporary barriers and ticket inspectors to bar access to the footbridge to non-ticket holders, and local residents and Supertram passengers were forced to use longer routes around the station.<sup id="cite_ref-ShefT090506_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShefT090506-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2009, East Midlands Trains were refused planning permission for the barriers by the council,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> but in February 2010 announced it would apply again.<sup id="cite_ref-ShefT100218_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShefT100218-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Transport Secretary <a href="/wiki/Lord_Adonis" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Adonis">Lord Adonis</a> announced in April 2010 that barriers would not be installed until a second bridge was built to maintain a thoroughfare for non-ticket holders.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From September 2010, East Midlands Trains used uniformed staff to prevent local residents using the footbridge.<sup id="cite_ref-yorkshirepost.co.uk_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yorkshirepost.co.uk-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> At the same time, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_City_Council" title="Sheffield City Council">Sheffield City Council</a> explored the possibility of turning the bridge into a public <a href="/wiki/Right_of_way_(public_throughway)" class="mw-redirect" title="Right of way (public throughway)">right-of-way</a> to resolve the matter. In late 2010, it was reported that the Deputy Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Nick_Clegg" title="Nick Clegg">Nick Clegg</a>, MP for <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Hallam_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Sheffield Hallam (UK Parliament constituency)">Sheffield Hallam</a>, might intervene to resolve the impasse.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2012, Transport Minister <a href="/wiki/Justine_Greening" title="Justine Greening">Justine Greening</a> offered £3 million to build a new footbridge to resolve the problem.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Tickets are not currently required to enter the station or to use the footbridge, which gives access to the Sheffield Station tram stop to the east.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future">Future</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ian Yeowart, former Managing Director of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Central_(train_operating_company)" title="Grand Central (train operating company)">Grand Central</a>, put forward in 2009 a bid for new open access <a href="/wiki/Alliance_Rail_Holdings" title="Alliance Rail Holdings">Alliance Rail Holdings</a> services operating on the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Modern_Railways_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Modern_Railways-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> As part of the scheme, four services a day would operate between Sheffield and <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">London King's Cross</a> via Alfreton, Nottingham and Grantham, meaning Sheffield would be connected to the capital by both the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Main_Line" title="Midland Main Line">Midland Main Line</a> and the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a> routes once again. Yeowart has proposed the resurrection of the name <a href="/wiki/Great_North_Eastern_Railway" title="Great North Eastern Railway">GNER</a> for the service, which has been unused since the last franchise of that name ended in 2007. However, in 2010 these proposed Sheffield to London Kings Cross services via the East Coast Main Line were rejected. In the 2010 Rail Utilisation Strategy, it quoted that the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Main_Line" title="Midland Main Line">Midland Main Line</a> north of <a href="/wiki/Bedford_railway_station" title="Bedford railway station">Bedford</a> will be electrified in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-Network_Rail_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Network_Rail-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The line is currently one of the few major main lines that is not electrified and the plan found that the project would provide significantly enhanced services and significant financial savings.<sup id="cite_ref-Network_Rail_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Network_Rail-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
In July 2017 Transport Secretary, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Grayling" title="Chris Grayling">Chris Grayling</a>, announced the electrification plan for the whole of the Midland Main Line would not go ahead as previously planned. Instead the section from Clay Cross in Derbyshire to Sheffield will be electrified by 2033 as part of the planned HS2. As an  interim measure bi-mode trains, claimed to offer benefits similar to high speed electric trains were to be used. A <a href="/wiki/National_Audit_Office_(United_Kingdom)" title="National Audit Office (United Kingdom)">National Audit Office</a> report said: “In the case of Midland Main Line, bi-mode trains with the required speed and acceleration did not exist when the Secretary of State made his decision." The MP for Loughborough (another area to have been served by the proposed electrification scheme) and Chair of the <a href="/wiki/Treasury_Select_Committee" title="Treasury Select Committee">Treasury Select Committee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicky_Morgan" title="Nicky Morgan">Nicky Morgan</a> said of the revised plans, "Now we see the decision to cancel it was based on fantasy trains that didn’t even exist and the Midlands being a guinea pig for an untested technology".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a>, aspiring to improve their overall network and services, aims to increase services between Sheffield and Leeds. East Midlands Trains also plans to make service improvements to its services between <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station" title="Liverpool Lime Street railway station">Liverpool</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwich_railway_station" title="Norwich railway station">Norwich</a> via Sheffield with two-car <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_158" title="British Rail Class 158">Class 158</a> trains doubling in capacity to four cars.<sup id="cite_ref-eastmidlandstrains.co.uk_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eastmidlandstrains.co.uk-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Coupled with newly acquired <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_156" title="British Rail Class 156">Class 156</a> trains, this will lead to an extra 1,500 seats being available each day on this service.<sup id="cite_ref-eastmidlandstrains.co.uk_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eastmidlandstrains.co.uk-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a>, responsible for operating most local services in the Sheffield area, announced in August 2011 that extra services between Sheffield and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Piccadilly railway station">Manchester Piccadilly</a> would begin in December that year. The <a href="/wiki/Hope_Valley_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Hope Valley Line">Hope Valley Line</a>, which will see an extra service in each direction during the peak evening period, is a key commuter route and currently has a two-hour gap in its evening schedule, which will be filled by the new services.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As part of the HS2 plans, a new platform would need to be constructed which would provide additional capacity for HS2, which approved the new route via Sheffield in July 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Four trains per hour are to serve Sheffield on the new high speed line. The work for HS2 will see the footprint of the station expand and major reconfiguration of the tram and roads surrounding the station to accommodate the extra services.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Station_Masters">Station Masters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Station Masters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul><li>Mr. Curtis 1870 - 1883 (formerly station master of Sheffield Wicker)</li>
<li>H.L. Wheen 1883<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> - 1905 (formerly station master at Bristol)</li>
<li>Shelton Chambers 1905<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> - 1911</li>
<li>J.L. Shannon 1911<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> - 1914 (formerly station master at Nottingham, afterwards station master at Derby)</li>
<li>George Preston Hegges 1914 - 1933 (formerly station master at Cheltenham Lansdown Road)</li>
<li>Frederick G. Hewitt 1933<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> - 1937 (afterwards station master of Birmingham New Street)</li>
<li>F.C. O’Connor 1937<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> -&#160;???? (formerly station master at Northampton)</li></ul>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable plainlinks">This list is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Lists#Incomplete_lists" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Lists">incomplete</a>; you can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sheffield_station&amp;action=edit">expanding it</a>.</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Station_facilities">Station facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Station facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The main station entrance, facing <a href="/wiki/Sheaf_Square" title="Sheaf Square">Sheaf Square</a>, is the location of the main concourse and most of the station's facilities. The ticket office, <a href="/wiki/Ticket_machine" title="Ticket machine">ticket machines</a>, information desk and a number of retail units are located there, and <a href="/wiki/Public_toilets" class="mw-redirect" title="Public toilets">public toilets</a> and facilities such as <a href="/wiki/Cash_machines" class="mw-redirect" title="Cash machines">cash machines</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Left_luggage" class="mw-redirect" title="Left luggage">left luggage</a> facility.<sup id="cite_ref-nationalrail.co.uk_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationalrail.co.uk-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> There are further shops and facilities on the island platforms and in the Supertram entrance hall at the far side of the station. There are waiting rooms on the island platforms and the East Midlands Trains first class lounge is within the station buildings, by platform 5.
</p><p>There is a 678-space <a href="/wiki/Car_park" class="mw-redirect" title="Car park">car park</a> situated next to the main station building (Q Park) and there is a reserved parking area for <a href="/wiki/Disabled_parking_permit" title="Disabled parking permit">blue badge</a> holders in the main station building.<sup id="cite_ref-nationalrail.co.uk_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationalrail.co.uk-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> There is also a <a href="/wiki/Taxi_rank" class="mw-redirect" title="Taxi rank">taxi rank</a> outside the station building, next to the disabled car park. Bicycle storage is provided on platforms 1a and 3a. The whole station, including platforms, concourse and Supertram stop, is accessible to disabled passengers.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Station_layout">Station layout</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Station layout">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td colspan="7" style="background:;text-align:;">
<div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><i>South &amp; Western routes</i><br />
&#32;<table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="font-size:90%;font-weight:inherit;color:inherit;background:transparent;margin-top:-2px;margin-bottom:-2px;display:inline-table;vertical-align:middle;text-align:inherit;font-style:italic;"><tbody><tr><td style="text-align:inherit;padding:0;line-height:.9;font-size:105%"><a href="/wiki/Midland_Main_Line" title="Midland Main Line">Midland Main Line</a> &amp; others</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:inherit;padding:0;line-height:.9;font-size:92%;font-style:italic">to <a href="/wiki/Southern_England" title="Southern England">the South</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/West_Midlands_(region)" title="West Midlands (region)">the West</a></td></tr></tbody></table>&#32;</div>

<p>The station is divided into four parts: the main building/<a href="/wiki/Concourse" title="Concourse">concourse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Railway_platform" title="Railway platform">platforms</a> 1a/1b; the first <a href="/wiki/Island_platform" title="Island platform">island</a> with platforms 2a-5b; the second island with platforms 6a-8b; and the adjoining Supertram stop. All sections are connected by a large <a href="/wiki/Footbridge" title="Footbridge">footbridge</a>.
</p><p>Sheffield station is designed to accommodate both through and terminating trains. Platforms 2c, 3, 4 and 7 can be used by terminating trains only.
The station has 9 platforms, numbered 1 to 8 and 2C. Platforms 1, 3 and 4 are divided into a and b sections to allow a brief stabling of terminating services before they are scheduled to depart. The station has four through roads which are used for through running or more commonly for stabling stock. Between platforms 5 and 6 these are known as "1-Up" and "2-Up" (they are on the "Up" or London-bound side of the station) whilst between platforms 1 and 2 are the "through road" with a direct path through the station or by a central crossover to the north end of platform 1 (1b), and "down station siding".
</p><p>Prior to the 1972 multiple-aspect signalling (MAS) scheme, the southern half of the current platform 8 was called platform 9. Trains from the north from platform 9 could avoid trains stood at platform 8 via an additional through road.
</p><p>The platforms are generally used as follows:
</p>
<ul><li>Platforms 1 and 2 - <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> to <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_railway_station" title="Huddersfield railway station">Huddersfield</a> (via <a href="/wiki/Barnsley_Interchange" title="Barnsley Interchange">Barnsley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Penistone_railway_station" title="Penistone railway station">Penistone</a>) and to Leeds via Barnsley (express); <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> to Cleethorpes; <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> to Newcastle and Scotland</li>
<li>Platform 2C - <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> stopping trains to Manchester Piccadilly</li>
<li>Platforms 3 and 4 - local stopping trains to Leeds (both routes), Lincoln,Adwick and Scarborough/Bridlington/Hull</li>
<li>Platform 5 - <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">East Midlands Railway</a> to London, Norwich and Nottingham; <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> to Birmingham, Reading and Exeter</li>
<li>Platform 6 - <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> to Birmingham, Reading and Exeter, <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> to <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Nottingham railway station">Nottingham</a> (via <a href="/wiki/Alfreton_railway_station" title="Alfreton railway station">Alfreton</a>), <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> to Manchester Airport</li>
<li>Platform 7 - <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">East Midlands Railway</a> to <a href="/wiki/Norwich_railway_station" title="Norwich railway station">Norwich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station" title="Liverpool Lime Street railway station">Liverpool</a></li>
<li>Platform 8 - <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">East Midlands Railway</a> to Manchester and Liverpool; <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">East Midlands Railway</a> to London.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Supertram_stop">Supertram stop</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Supertram stop">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em;width: 25.5em;"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold"><div style="display: table; width: 100%; border-collapse: collapse"><div style="display: table-cell; width: inherit; vertical-align: middle"><div style="display:inline" class="fn org">Sheffield Station / Sheffield Hallam University</div></div></div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="category" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Supertram" title="Sheffield Supertram">Sheffield Supertram</a> station</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Station_Tram_Stop_-_geograph.org.uk_-_724214.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Sheffield Station Tram Stop - geograph.org.uk - 724214.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Sheffield_Station_Tram_Stop_-_geograph.org.uk_-_724214.jpg/300px-Sheffield_Station_Tram_Stop_-_geograph.org.uk_-_724214.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="201" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Sheffield_Station_Tram_Stop_-_geograph.org.uk_-_724214.jpg/450px-Sheffield_Station_Tram_Stop_-_geograph.org.uk_-_724214.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Sheffield_Station_Tram_Stop_-_geograph.org.uk_-_724214.jpg/600px-Sheffield_Station_Tram_Stop_-_geograph.org.uk_-_724214.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="428" /></a><div>The tram stop in 2008. The mainline station is behind the cream wall to the left of the tram.</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Location</th><td class="label">Granville Street, Park Hill, Sheffield</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Coordinates</th><td><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Sheffield_station&amp;params=53_22_40_N_1_27_40.6_W_region:GB_type:railwaystation"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">53°22′40″N</span> <span class="longitude">1°27′40.6″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">53.37778°N 1.461278°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">53.37778; -1.461278</span></span></span></a></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Owned by</th><td><a href="/wiki/South_Yorkshire_Passenger_Transport_Executive" title="South Yorkshire Passenger Transport Executive">Travel South Yorkshire</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Line(s)</th><td>Blue Route<br />Purple Route</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Platforms</th><td>2 in use<br /><small>Plus 3 from original station retained for additional capacity when required</small></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Tracks</th><td>2</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#efefef">Construction</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Structure type</th><td>Embankment</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Platform levels</th><td>1</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Parking</th><td>No</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Bicycle facilities</th><td>No</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Disabled access</th><td>Yes</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#efefef">Other information</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Station code</th><td class="nickname">SHS</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#efefef">History</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Opened</th><td>1994</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Rebuilt</th><td>2002</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Electrified</th><td>Yes</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Sheffield Station / Sheffield Hallam University</b> stop on the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Supertram" title="Sheffield Supertram">Sheffield Supertram</a> has direct interchange with Sheffield railway station. The station is built on top of a walled <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/embankment" class="extiw" title="wikt:embankment">embankment</a> high above platform 8 on the eastern side of the station; this embankment formerly carried Granville Street past the station, which was downgraded to a lineside public footpath when the embankment was repurposed to carry the Supertram line past the station in the early 1990s. In addition to the mainline station, the stop also serves the City Campus of <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Hallam_University" title="Sheffield Hallam University">Sheffield Hallam University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Park_Hill,_Sheffield" title="Park Hill, Sheffield">Park Hill estate</a> above the railway station.
</p><p>The original stop opened in 1994 with the rest of the network. The original stop had three platforms - two on the northbound (inbound to the city centre) track, to allow for terminating Purple Route services prior to their extension to Cathedral in the city centre - and was connected to platform 6 of the main station by a simple staircase.
</p><p>In line with the refurbishment of the rest of the station in the early 2000s, the tram stop was rebuilt in 2002 around 150 metres to the south of the existing platforms. As well as two new platforms, a ticket hall was constructed at the end of the main station footbridge over the top of platform 8, providing a direct connection from the tram stop to the station footbridge and the rest of the mainline station. Following the opening of the new stop, the old platforms were left in situ but have only ever been used in recent years in times of engineering works where additional platform space has been required.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Trains per hour:
</p><p><b>East Midlands Railway</b><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>2 to <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">London St Pancras</a> via <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_railway_station" title="Chesterfield railway station">Chesterfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derby_railway_station" title="Derby railway station">Derby</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Leicester_railway_station" title="Leicester railway station">Leicester</a>. Three named passenger trains (The <i><a href="/wiki/Master_Cutler_(train)" title="Master Cutler (train)">Master Cutler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Continental" title="Sheffield Continental">Sheffield Continental</a></i> &amp; <i><a href="/wiki/South_Yorkshireman" title="South Yorkshireman">South Yorkshireman</a></i>) run on this service.</li>
<li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Norwich_railway_station" title="Norwich railway station">Norwich</a> via <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Nottingham railway station">Nottingham</a>.</li>
<li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Lime_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverpool Lime Street">Liverpool Lime Street</a> via <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Piccadilly">Manchester Piccadilly</a>.</li></ul>
<p><b>CrossCountry</b><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Waverley_railway_station" title="Edinburgh Waverley railway station">Edinburgh Waverley</a> via <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station" title="Newcastle railway station">Newcastle</a>. Some trains continue on to <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Central railway station">Glasgow Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dundee_railway_station" title="Dundee railway station">Dundee</a> or <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_railway_station" title="Aberdeen railway station">Aberdeen</a>.</li>
<li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station" title="Newcastle railway station">Newcastle</a> via <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_railway_station" title="Doncaster railway station">Doncaster</a> and <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a>.</li>
<li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_railway_station" title="Plymouth railway station">Plymouth</a> via <a href="/wiki/Derby_railway_station" title="Derby railway station">Derby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_New_Street_railway_station" title="Birmingham New Street railway station">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Temple_Meads_railway_station" title="Bristol Temple Meads railway station">Bristol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Exeter_St_Davids_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter St Davids railway station">Exeter</a>, with some trains extending through to <a href="/wiki/Penzance_railway_station" title="Penzance railway station">Penzance</a>.</li>
<li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Reading_railway_station" title="Reading railway station">Reading</a> via Derby, Birmingham and <a href="/wiki/Oxford_railway_station" title="Oxford railway station">Oxford</a>, with some trains extending through to <a href="/wiki/Southampton_Central_railway_station" title="Southampton Central railway station">Southampton Central</a>.</li></ul>
<p><b>TransPennine Express</b><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Airport railway station">Manchester Airport</a> via <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Piccadilly railway station">Manchester Piccadilly</a>.</li>
<li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Cleethorpes_railway_station" title="Cleethorpes railway station">Cleethorpes</a> via <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_railway_station" title="Doncaster railway station">Doncaster</a>.</li></ul>
<p><b>Northern</b><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Piccadilly railway station">Manchester Piccadilly</a> via <a href="/wiki/New_Mills_Central_railway_station" title="New Mills Central railway station">New Mills</a>.</li>
<li>2 to <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a> via <a href="/wiki/Barnsley_Interchange" title="Barnsley Interchange">Barnsley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Kirkgate_railway_station" title="Wakefield Kirkgate railway station">Wakefield</a> (fast).</li>
<li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a> via Barnsley, Wakefield and <a href="/wiki/Castleford_railway_station" title="Castleford railway station">Castleford</a> (stopping).</li>
<li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a> via <a href="/wiki/Moorthorpe_railway_station" title="Moorthorpe railway station">Moorthorpe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Westgate_railway_station" title="Wakefield Westgate railway station">Wakefield</a>.</li>
<li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Nottingham railway station">Nottingham</a> via Chesterfield.</li>
<li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Bridlington_railway_station" title="Bridlington railway station">Bridlington</a> via <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_railway_station" title="Doncaster railway station">Doncaster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hull_Paragon_Interchange" title="Hull Paragon Interchange">Hull</a> (fast).</li>
<li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Central_railway_station" title="Lincoln Central railway station">Lincoln</a> Central via <a href="/wiki/Worksop_railway_station" title="Worksop railway station">Worksop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Retford_railway_station" title="Retford railway station">Retford</a>.</li>
<li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Gainsborough_Central_railway_station" title="Gainsborough Central railway station">Gainsborough Central</a> via <a href="/wiki/Worksop_railway_station" title="Worksop railway station">Worksop</a>, three trains per week continue to <a href="/wiki/Cleethorpes_railway_station" title="Cleethorpes railway station">Cleethorpes</a> via <a href="/wiki/Brigg_railway_station" title="Brigg railway station">Brigg</a>.</li>
<li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_railway_station" title="Huddersfield railway station">Huddersfield</a> via <a href="/wiki/Meadowhall_Interchange" title="Meadowhall Interchange">Meadowhall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barnsley_Interchange" title="Barnsley Interchange">Barnsley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Penistone_railway_station" title="Penistone railway station">Penistone</a></li>
<li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Hull_Paragon_Interchange" title="Hull Paragon Interchange">Hull</a> via <a href="/wiki/Meadowhall_Interchange" title="Meadowhall Interchange">Meadowhall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_railway_station" title="Doncaster railway station">Doncaster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Goole_railway_station" title="Goole railway station">Goole</a> (stopping).</li>
<li>1 to <a href="/wiki/Adwick_railway_station" title="Adwick railway station">Adwick</a> via Meadowhall and Doncaster.</li>
<li>2 trains per day to <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a> via Moorthorpe and <a href="/wiki/Sherburn-in-Elmet_railway_station" title="Sherburn-in-Elmet railway station">Sherburn-in-Elmet</a>.</li></ul>
<p><b>HS2 Services</b>
</p><p>HS2 will see a spur south of Chesterfield branch off the Main Route, which will go via the M18, allowing trains to head into a stop at Chesterfield and also head to Sheffield via the Sheffield to Leeds Line.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
